To ensure the accuracy of assembly, the scaffold misjoins, ordering, and orientation were further checked and corrected manually based on the interaction matrix of scaffolds from the Juicebox visualization system<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicebox provides a visualization system for Hi-C contact maps with unlimited zoom. Cell Syst. 3, 99–101 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1301">57</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec11">Comparison of genetic map and physical map</h3><p>To assess the CSS V1.2 genome, two public genetic maps<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Ma, J. Q. et al. Large-scale SNP discovery and genotyping for constructing a high-density genetic map of tea plant using Specific-Locus Amplified Fragment Sequencing (SLAF-seq). PLoS ONE 10, e0128798 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1313">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Xu, L. Y. et al. High-density SNP linkage map construction and QTL mapping for flavonoid-related traits in a tea plant (Camellia sinensis) using 2b-RAD sequencing. BMC Genomics 19, 955 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1316">41</a></sup> were used for collinearity analysis compared with the chromosome-scale assembly. A total of 6042 valid SNP markers of a SLAF-seq genetic map (F1 population, CSS ‘Yingshuang’ × <i>C. sinensis</i> var. <i>pubilimba</i> ‘Beiyue Danzhu’)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Ma, J. Q. et al. Large-scale SNP discovery and genotyping for constructing a high-density genetic map of tea plant using Specific-Locus Amplified Fragment Sequencing (SLAF-seq). PLoS ONE 10, e0128798 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1326">22</a></sup> and 2380 available markers of a 2b-RAD genetic map (F1 population, CSS ‘Longjing 43’ × CSS ‘Baihaozao’)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Xu, L. Y. et al. High-density SNP linkage map construction and QTL mapping for flavonoid-related traits in a tea plant (Camellia sinensis) using 2b-RAD sequencing. BMC Genomics 19, 955 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1330">41</a></sup> were aligned to the assembled genome by Bowtie (version 1.2.1.1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Langmead, B., Trapnell, C., Pop, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Ultrafast and memory-efficient alignment of short DNA sequences to the human genome. Genome Biol. 10, R25 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1335">58</a></sup> with ‘-a –v 1’ parameters. To obtain unambiguous alignments, reads that mapped to more than two places in the genome were removed. The dotplot of collinearity comparison was drawn by Perl script with the SVG module.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec12">Analysis of WGD and tandem duplication</h3><p>Genes anchored to chromosomes in the <i>C. sinensis</i>, <i>V. vinifera</i>, and <i>A. chinensis</i> genomes were used to analyze genome evolution. First, protein sequences of <i>C. sinensis</i> were searched against the three genomes to find potentially homologous genes using BLASTP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Altschul, S. F. et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 3389–3402 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1359">59</a></sup> (<i>e</i>-value threshold, 1e−5). Second, large gene families with &gt;30 matches were filtered out, and the remaining homologous genes were used for inferring homologous blocks by MCScanX<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, e49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1367">60</a></sup> software with ‘-s 4 –m 50 –w 5’ parameters. The synonymous nucleotide substitution rates (<i>K</i>s) were calculated by using <i>add_ka_and_ks_to_collinearity.pl</i> implemented in MCScanX.</p><p>To distinguish the event-related homologous blocks, homologous blocks between the <i>C. sinensis</i> and <i>V. vinifera</i> genomes attributable to WGD events occurring after the tea-grape split were identified by the criterion that the best-matched homologous gene pairs accounted for &gt;50% in a homologous block. To identify the ECH and CRT events in the <i>C. sinensis</i> genome, any homologous block with median <i>K</i>s &gt; 0.7 was defined as an ECH event, and any other was defined as a CRT event. The smooth curve of <i>K</i>s distribution was obtained by using the Gaussian kernel function.</p><p>To identify tandem duplications, all genes anchored to the chromosomes were compared by BLASTP to find homologous genes (<i>e</i>-value &lt; 1e−20). The homologous genes with a maximum of five intervening genes were defined as tandem duplicates<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Myburg, A. A. et al. The genome of Eucalyptus grandis. Nature 510, 356–362 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1401">61</a></sup>. KEGG enrichment analysis of tandem duplicates was performed by clusterProfiler package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Yu, G., Wang, L. G., Han, Y. &amp; He, Q. Y. clusterProfiler: an R package for comparing biological themes among gene clusters. OMICS 16, 284–287 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1405">62</a></sup> with the cutoff set at adjusted <i>P</i> value &lt; 0.05.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec13">RNA-seq data analysis</h3><p>The RNA-seq data of eight tissues (apical bud, young leaf, mature leaf, old leaf, young stem, root, flower, and fruit) of CSS ‘Shuchazao’ were obtained from the NCBI SRA database submitted by Wei et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Wei, C. et al. Draft genome sequence of Camellia sinensis var. sinensis provides insights into the evolution of the tea genome and tea quality. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 115, E4151–E4158 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1421">13</a></sup> (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#MOESM1">9</a>). The raw Illumina reads were trimmed by Trimmomatic (v 0.36)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Bolger, A. M., Lohse, M. &amp; Usadel, B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics 30, 2114–2120 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1428">63</a></sup> and then aligned to the CSS V1.2 reference genome using HISAT2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Kim, D., Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods 12, 357–360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1432">64</a></sup> with default settings. Differential expression between duplicate genes was calculated by the edgeR package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Robinson, M. D., McCarthy, D. J. &amp; Smyth, G. K. edgeR: a Bioconductor package for differential expression analysis of digital gene expression data. Bioinformatics 26, 139–140 (2010)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1436">65</a></sup> with an FDR &lt; 0.05 and at least a two-fold difference in expression levels.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Identification of NBS genes</h3><p>All genes from the <i>C. sinensis</i> genome were annotated using HMMER 3.1b2 (<a href="http://hmmer.org/">http://hmmer.org/</a>) against the Pfam database with an <i>e</i>-value threshold of 0.001. Genes with NB-ARC domains (PF00931) were defined as NBS genes and used for further analysis. These NBS genes were classified by different conserved domains identified by Pfam and the NCBI Conserved Domains Tool<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Marchler-Bauer, A. et al. CDD: a Conserved Domain Database for the functional annotation of proteins. Nucleic Acids Res. 39, D225–D229 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1458">66</a></sup>. The conserved domains were confirmed using the following accession numbers: TIR (PF13676, PF01582), LRR (PF00560, PF07723, PF07725, PF12799, PF13306, PF13516, PF13504, PF13855, cl34836), and RPW8 (PF05659). CC domains were detected and confirmed by Paircoil2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="McDonnell, A. V., Jiang, T., Keating, A. E. &amp; Berger, B. Paircoil2: improved prediction of coiled coils from sequence. Bioinformatics 22, 356–358 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-0288-2#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d4353e1462">67</a></sup> with a <i>P</i>-score cutoff of 0.025.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The raw Hi-C data of CSS ‘Shuchazao’ have been deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under BioProject accession no. PRJNA596054. The CSS V1.2 assembly data is available at <a href="https://github.com/JiedanChen/TeaGenomeData">https://github.com/JiedanChen/TeaGenomeData</a>.</p>
